<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Conf_dead_chancellorsville_edit1.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1894" data-file-width="2184" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Conf_dead_chancellorsville_edit1.jpg/180px-Conf_dead_chancellorsville_edit1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Conf_dead_chancellorsville_edit1.jpg/270px-Conf_dead_chancellorsville_edit1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Conf_dead_chancellorsville_edit1.jpg/360px-Conf_dead_chancellorsville_edit1.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Confederate dead overrun at Marye's Heights, reoccupied next day May 4, 1863</div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>When the Emancipation Proclamation went into effect in January 1863, ex-slaves were energetically recruited by the states, and used to meet the state quotas. States and local communities offered higher and higher cash bonuses for white volunteers. Congress tightened the law in March 1863. Men selected in the draft could provide substitutes or, until mid-1864, pay commutation money. Many eligibles pooled their money to cover the cost of anyone drafted. Families used the substitute provision to select which man should go into the army and which should stay home. There was much evasion and overt resistance to the draft, especially in Catholic areas. The great <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_York_Draft_Riots" title="New York Draft Riots">draft riot in New York City in July 1863</a> involved Irish immigrants who had been signed up as citizens to swell the vote of the <a href="/wiki/Tammany_Hall" title="Tammany Hall">city's Democratic political machine</a>, not realizing it made them liable for the draft.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reconstruct_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-reconstruct-118">[116]</a></sup> Of the 168,649 men procured for the Union through the draft, 117,986 were substitutes, leaving only 50,663 who had their personal services conscripted.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-murdock_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-murdock-119">[117]</a></sup></p>
<p>In both the North and South, the draft laws were highly unpopular. In the North, some 120,000 men evaded conscription, many of them fleeing to Canada, and another 280,000 soldiers deserted during the war.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[118]</a></sup> At least 100,000 Southerners deserted, or about 10 percent. In the South, many men deserted temporarily to take care of their distressed families, then returned to their units.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[119]</a></sup> In the North, "bounty jumpers" enlisted to get the generous bonus, deserted, then went back to a second recruiting station under a different name to sign up again for a second bonus; 141 were caught and executed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-desertion37_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-desertion37-122">[120]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NYRiot.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="599" data-file-width="478" height="213" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/NYRiot.jpg/170px-NYRiot.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/NYRiot.jpg/255px-NYRiot.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/NYRiot.jpg/340px-NYRiot.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NYRiot.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Rioters attacking a building during the <a href="/wiki/New_York_City_draft_riots" title="New York City draft riots">New York anti-draft riots</a> of 1863</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>From a tiny frontier force in 1860, the Union and Confederate armies had grown into the "largest and most efficient armies in the world" within a few years. European observers at the time dismissed them as amateur and unprofessional, but British historian <a href="/wiki/John_Keegan" title="John Keegan">John Keegan</a>'s assessment is that each outmatched the French, Prussian and Russian armies of the time, and but for the Atlantic, would have threatened any of them with defeat.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKeegan200957_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKeegan200957-123">[121]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Motivation">Motivation</span></h4>
<p>Perman and Taylor (2010) say that historians are of two minds on why millions of men seemed so eager to fight, suffer and die over four years:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>Some historians emphasize that Civil War soldiers were driven by political ideology, holding firm beliefs about the importance of liberty, Union, or state rights, or about the need to protect or to destroy slavery. Others point to less overtly political reasons to fight, such as the defense of one's home and family, or the honor and brotherhood to be preserved when fighting alongside other men. Most historians agree that no matter what a soldier thought about when he went into the war, the experience of combat affected him profoundly and sometimes altered his reasons for continuing the fight.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPermanTaylor2010177_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPermanTaylor2010177-124">[122]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Prisoners">Prisoners</span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War_prison_camps" title="American Civil War prison camps">American Civil War prison camps</a></div>
<p>At the start of the civil war, a system of paroles operated. Captives agreed not to fight until they were officially exchanged. Meanwhile, they were held in camps run by their own army where they were paid but not allowed to perform any military duties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[123]</a></sup> The system of exchanges collapsed in 1863 when the Confederacy refused to exchange black prisoners. After that, about 56,000 of the 409,000 POWs died in prisons during the war, accounting for nearly 10 percent of the conflict's fatalities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETuckerPierpaoliWhite20101466_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETuckerPierpaoliWhite20101466-126">[124]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Naval_war">Naval war</span></h3>
<p>The small <a href="/wiki/Union_Navy" title="Union Navy">U.S. Navy</a> of 1861 was rapidly enlarged to 6,000 officers and 45,000 men in 1865, with 671 vessels, having a tonnage of 510,396.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWelles1865152_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWelles1865152-127">[125]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETuckerPierpaoliWhite2010462_128-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETuckerPierpaoliWhite2010462-128">[126]</a></sup> Its mission was to blockade Confederate ports, take control of the river system, defend against Confederate raiders on the high seas, and be ready for a possible war with the British <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECanney1998.3F_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECanney1998.3F-129">[127]</a></sup> Meanwhile, the main riverine war was fought in the West, where a series of major rivers gave access to the Confederate heartland, if the U.S. Navy could take control. In the East, the Navy supplied and moved army forces about, and occasionally shelled Confederate installations.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Union_blockade">Union blockade</span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Union_blockade" title="Union blockade">Union blockade</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Scott-anaconda.jpg"><img alt="A cartoon map of the South surrounded by a snake." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4382" data-file-width="5248" height="276" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Scott-anaconda.jpg/330px-Scott-anaconda.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Scott-anaconda.jpg/495px-Scott-anaconda.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Scott-anaconda.jpg/660px-Scott-anaconda.jpg 2x" width="330"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Scott-anaconda.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
General Scott's "<a href="/wiki/Anaconda_Plan" title="Anaconda Plan">Anaconda Plan</a>" 1861. Tightening naval blockade, forcing rebels out of Missouri along the Mississippi River, Kentucky Unionists sit on the fence, idled cotton industry illustrated in Georgia.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>By early 1861, General <a href="/wiki/Winfield_Scott" title="Winfield Scott">Winfield Scott</a> had devised the <a href="/wiki/Anaconda_Plan" title="Anaconda Plan">Anaconda Plan</a> to win the war with as little bloodshed as possible.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERichter200949_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERichter200949-130">[128]</a></sup> Scott argued that a Union blockade of the main ports would weaken the Confederate economy. Lincoln adopted parts of the plan, but he overruled Scott's caution about 90-day volunteers. Public opinion, however, demanded an immediate attack by the army to capture Richmond.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJohnson1998228_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJohnson1998228-131">[129]</a></sup></p>
<p>In April 1861, Lincoln announced the Union blockade of all Southern ports; commercial ships could not get insurance and regular traffic ended. The South blundered in embargoing cotton exports in 1861 before the blockade was effective; by the time they realized the mistake, it was too late. "King Cotton" was dead, as the South could export less than 10 percent of its cotton. The blockade shut down the ten Confederate seaports with railheads that moved almost all the cotton, especially New Orleans, Mobile, and Charleston. By June 1861, warships were stationed off the principal Southern ports, and a year later nearly 300 ships were in service.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAnderson1989288.E2.80.9389.2C_296.E2.80.9398_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAnderson1989288.E2.80.9389.2C_296.E2.80.9398-132">[130]</a></sup></p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_navy_evolves">Modern navy evolves</span></h5>
<p>The Civil War occurred during the early stages of the industrial revolution and subsequently many naval innovations emerged during this time, most notably the advent of the <a href="/wiki/Ironclad_warship" title="Ironclad warship">ironclad warship</a>. It began when the Confederacy, knowing they had to meet or match the Union's naval superiority, responded to the Union blockade by building or converting more than 130 vessels, including twenty-six ironclads and floating batteries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENelson200592_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENelson200592-133">[131]</a></sup> Only half of these saw active service. Many were equipped with ram bows, creating "ram fever" among Union squadrons wherever they threatened. But in the face of overwhelming Union superiority and the Union's own ironclad warships, they were unsuccessful.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAnderson1989300_134-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAnderson1989300-134">[132]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Confederacy experimented with a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CSS_Hunley" title="CSS Hunley">submarine</a>, which did not work well,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[133]</a></sup> and with building an ironclad ship, the <a href="/wiki/CSS_Virginia" title="CSS Virginia">CSS <i>Virginia</i></a>, which was based on rebuilding a sunken Union ship, the <a href="/wiki/USS_Merrimack_(1855)" title="USS Merrimack (1855)"><i>Merrimack</i></a>. On its first foray on March 8, 1862, the <i>Virginia</i> inflicted significant damage to the Union's wooden fleet, but the next day the first Union ironclad, the <a href="/wiki/USS_Monitor" title="USS Monitor">USS <i>Monitor</i></a>, arrived to challenge it in the <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake_Bay" title="Chesapeake Bay">Chesapeake Bay</a>. The resulting three hour <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Hampton_Roads" title="Battle of Hampton Roads">battle between the Ironclads</a> was a draw, but it marked the worldwide transition to ironclad warships.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENelson2005345_136-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENelson2005345-136">[134]</a></sup> Not long after the battle the Confederacy was forced to scuttle the <i>Virginia</i> to prevent its capture, while the Union built many copies of the <i>Monitor</i>. Lacking the technology and infrastructure to build effective warships, the Confederacy attempted to obtain warships from Britain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFuller200836_137-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFuller200836-137">[135]</a></sup></p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Blockade_runners">Blockade runners</span></h5>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Blockade_runners_of_the_American_Civil_War" title="Blockade runners of the American Civil War">Blockade runners of the American Civil War</a></div>
<p>British investors built small, fast, steam-driven <a href="/wiki/Blockade_runners_of_the_American_Civil_War" title="Blockade runners of the American Civil War">blockade runners</a> that traded arms and luxuries brought in from Britain through Bermuda, Cuba, and the Bahamas in return for high-priced cotton. Many of the ships were designed for speed and were so small that only a small amount of cotton went out.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEStern1962224-225_138-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEStern1962224-225-138">[136]</a></sup> When the Union Navy seized a blockade runner, the ship and cargo were condemned as a <a href="/wiki/Prize_of_war" title="Prize of war">Prize of war</a> and sold, with the proceeds given to the Navy sailors; the captured crewmen were mostly British and they were simply released.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[137]</a></sup> The Southern economy nearly collapsed during the war. There were multiple reasons for this: the severe deterioration of food supplies, especially in cities, the failure of Southern railroads, the loss of control of the main rivers, foraging by Northern armies, and the seizure of animals and crops by Confederate armies. Most historians agree that the blockade was a major factor in ruining the Confederate economy; however, Wise argues that the blockade runners provided just enough of a lifeline to allow Lee to continue fighting for additional months, thanks to fresh supplies of 400,000 rifles, lead, blankets, and boots that the homefront economy could no longer supply.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[138]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:First_Charleston_Harbor.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="350" data-file-width="900" height="101" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/First_Charleston_Harbor.jpg/260px-First_Charleston_Harbor.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/First_Charleston_Harbor.jpg/390px-First_Charleston_Harbor.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/First_Charleston_Harbor.jpg/520px-First_Charleston_Harbor.jpg 2x" width="260"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:First_Charleston_Harbor.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Gunline of nine Union ironclads. <a href="/wiki/Union_blockade#South_Atlantic_Blockading_Squadron" title="Union blockade">South Atlantic Blockading Squadron</a> off Charleston. Continuous blockade of all major ports was sustained by North's overwhelming war production.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Economic_impact">Economic impact</span></h5>
<p>Surdam argues that the blockade was a powerful weapon that eventually ruined the Southern economy, at the cost of few lives in combat. Practically, the entire Confederate cotton crop was useless (although it was sold to Union traders), costing the Confederacy its main source of income. Critical imports were scarce and the coastal trade was largely ended as well.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[139]</a></sup> The measure of the blockade's success was not the few ships that slipped through, but the thousands that never tried it. Merchant ships owned in Europe could not get insurance and were too slow to evade the blockade; they simply stopped calling at Confederate ports.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[140]</a></sup></p>
<p>To fight an offensive war, the Confederacy purchased ships from Britain, converted them to warships, and raided American merchant ships in the Atlantic and Pacific oceans. Insurance rates skyrocketed and the American flag virtually disappeared from international waters. However, the same ships were reflagged with European flags and continued unmolested.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAnderson1989300_134-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAnderson1989300-134">[132]</a></sup> After the war, the U.S. demanded that Britain pay for the damage done, and Britain paid the U.S. $15 million in 1871.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJones2002225_143-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJones2002225-143">[141]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Rivers">Rivers</span></h4>
<p>The 1862 Union strategy called for simultaneous advances along four axes:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAnderson198991_144-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAnderson198991-144">[142]</a></sup></p>
<ol>
<li>McClellan would lead the main thrust in Virginia towards Richmond.</li>
<li>Ohio forces would advance through Kentucky into Tennessee.</li>
<li>The Missouri Department would drive south along the Mississippi River.</li>
<li>The westernmost attack would originate from Kansas.</li>
</ol>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:322px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NavalBattleOfFortPillow.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="428" data-file-width="740" height="185" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/NavalBattleOfFortPillow.jpg/320px-NavalBattleOfFortPillow.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/NavalBattleOfFortPillow.jpg/480px-NavalBattleOfFortPillow.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/NavalBattleOfFortPillow.jpg/640px-NavalBattleOfFortPillow.jpg 2x" width="320"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NavalBattleOfFortPillow.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<div class="center" style="width:auto; margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;">Clashes on the rivers were melees of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ironclads" title="Ironclads">ironclads</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cottonclad_warship" title="Cottonclad warship">cottonclads</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gunboats" title="Gunboats">gunboats</a> and rams, complicated by torpedoes and by <a href="/wiki/Fire_ship" title="Fire ship">fire rafts</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Ulysses_S._Grant" title="Ulysses S. Grant">Ulysses Grant</a> used river transport and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Andrew_H._Foote" title="Andrew H. Foote">Andrew Foote's</a> gunboats of the Western Flotilla to threaten the Confederacy's "Gibraltar of the West" at Columbus, Kentucky. Though rebuffed at Belmont, Grant cut off Columbus. The Confederates, lacking their own gunboats, were forced to retreat and the Union took control of western Kentucky in March 1862.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[143]</a></sup></p>
<p>In addition to ocean-going warships coming up the Mississippi, the Union Navy used timberclads, tinclads, and armored gunboats. Shipyards at Cairo, Illinois, and St. Louis built new boats or modified steamboats for action.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[144]</a></sup> They took control of the Red, Tennessee, Cumberland, Mississippi, and Ohio rivers after victories at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Fort_Henry" title="Battle of Fort Henry">Fort Henry</a> (February 6, 1862) and <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Fort_Donelson" title="Battle of Fort Donelson">Fort Donelson</a> (February 11 to 16, 1862), and supplied Grant's forces as he moved into Tennessee. At <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Shiloh" title="Battle of Shiloh">Shiloh</a> (Pittsburg Landing), in Tennessee in April 1862, the Confederates made a surprise attack that pushed Union forces against the river as night fell. Overnight, the Navy landed additional reinforcements, and Grant counter-attacked. Grant and the Union won a decisive victoryâthe first battle with the high casualty rates that would repeat over and over.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFrankReaves2003170_147-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFrankReaves2003170-147">[145]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battle_of_Memphis" title="Battle of Memphis">Memphis fell to Union forces</a> on June 6, 1862, and became a key base for further advances south along the Mississippi River. On April 24, 1862, U.S. Naval forces under <a href="/wiki/David_Farragut" title="David Farragut">Farragut</a> ran past Confederate defenses south of New Orleans. Confederate forces abandoned the city, giving the Union a critical anchor in the deep South.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESymondsClipson200192_148-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESymondsClipson200192-148">[146]</a></sup></p>
<p>Naval forces assisted Grant in the long, complex <a href="/wiki/Vicksburg_Campaign" title="Vicksburg Campaign">Vicksburg Campaign</a> that resulted in the Confederates surrendering at <a href="/wiki/Vicksburg,_Mississippi" title="Vicksburg, Mississippi">Vicksburg, Mississippi</a> in July 1863, and in the Union fully controlling the Mississippi River soon after.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[147]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Eastern_theater">Eastern theater</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">For more details on this topic, see <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Theater_of_the_American_Civil_War" title="Eastern Theater of the American Civil War">Eastern Theater of the American Civil War</a>.</div>
<p>In one of the first highly visible battles, a march by Union troops under the command of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Major_General" title="Major General">Maj. Gen.</a> <a href="/wiki/Irvin_McDowell" title="Irvin McDowell">Irvin McDowell</a> on the Confederate forces near Washington was repulsed.</p>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:448px;max-width:448px">
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:222px;max-width:222px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Antietam_by_Thulstrup.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="460" data-file-width="663" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Battle_of_Antietam_by_Thulstrup.jpg/220px-Battle_of_Antietam_by_Thulstrup.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Battle_of_Antietam_by_Thulstrup.jpg/330px-Battle_of_Antietam_by_Thulstrup.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Battle_of_Antietam_by_Thulstrup.jpg/440px-Battle_of_Antietam_by_Thulstrup.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:222px;max-width:222px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Hampton_Roads_3g01752u.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1229" data-file-width="1736" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Battle_of_Hampton_Roads_3g01752u.jpg/220px-Battle_of_Hampton_Roads_3g01752u.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Battle_of_Hampton_Roads_3g01752u.jpg/330px-Battle_of_Hampton_Roads_3g01752u.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Battle_of_Hampton_Roads_3g01752u.jpg/440px-Battle_of_Hampton_Roads_3g01752u.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a></div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent">
<div class="center" style="width:auto; margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;">Left: The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Antietam" title="Battle of Antietam">Battle of Antietam</a>, the Civil War's deadliest one-day fight. Union troops committed piecemeal had little effect.</div>
<div class="center" style="width:auto; margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;">Right: Confederate ironclads at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Hampton_Roads" title="Battle of Hampton Roads">Norfolk</a> and New Orleans dispersed blockade, until Union ironclads could defeat them.</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Maj. Gen. <a href="/wiki/George_B._McClellan" title="George B. McClellan">George B. McClellan</a> took command of the Union <a href="/wiki/Army_of_the_Potomac" title="Army of the Potomac">Army of the Potomac</a> on July 26 (he was briefly general-in-chief of all the Union armies, but was subsequently relieved of that post in favor of Maj. Gen. <a href="/wiki/Henry_Halleck" title="Henry Halleck">Henry W. Halleck</a>), and the war began in earnest in 1862. Upon the strong urging of President Lincoln to begin offensive operations, McClellan attacked Virginia in the spring of 1862 by way of the <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Peninsula" title="Virginia Peninsula">peninsula</a> between the <a href="/wiki/York_River_(Virginia)" title="York River (Virginia)">York River</a> and <a href="/wiki/James_River" title="James River">James River</a>, southeast of Richmond. Although McClellan's army reached the gates of Richmond in the <a href="/wiki/Peninsula_Campaign" title="Peninsula Campaign">Peninsula Campaign</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFoote1974464.E2.80.93519_150-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFoote1974464.E2.80.93519-150">[148]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-terrible_151-0"><a href="#cite_note-terrible-151">[149]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcPherson1988424.E2.80.9327_152-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcPherson1988424.E2.80.9327-152">[150]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Joseph_E._Johnston" title="Joseph E. Johnston">Johnston</a> halted his advance at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Seven_Pines" title="Battle of Seven Pines">Battle of Seven Pines</a>, then General <a href="/wiki/Robert_E._Lee" title="Robert E. Lee">Robert E. Lee</a> and top subordinates <a href="/wiki/James_Longstreet" title="James Longstreet">James Longstreet</a> and Stonewall Jackson defeated McClellan in the <a href="/wiki/Seven_Days_Battles" title="Seven Days Battles">Seven Days Battles</a> and forced his retreat.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcPherson1988538.E2.80.9344_153-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcPherson1988538.E2.80.9344-153">[151]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Northern_Virginia_Campaign" title="Northern Virginia Campaign">Northern Virginia Campaign</a>, which included the <a href="/wiki/Second_Battle_of_Bull_Run" title="Second Battle of Bull Run">Second Battle of Bull Run</a>, ended in yet another victory for the South.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcPherson1988528.E2.80.9333_154-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcPherson1988528.E2.80.9333-154">[152]</a></sup> McClellan resisted General-in-Chief Halleck's orders to send reinforcements to <a href="/wiki/John_Pope_(military_officer)" title="John Pope (military officer)">John Pope's</a> Union <a href="/wiki/Army_of_Virginia" title="Army of Virginia">Army of Virginia</a>, which made it easier for Lee's Confederates to defeat twice the number of combined enemy troops.</p>
<p>Emboldened by Second Bull Run, the Confederacy made its first invasion of the North. General Lee led 45,000 men of the <a href="/wiki/Army_of_Northern_Virginia" title="Army of Northern Virginia">Army of Northern Virginia</a> across the <a href="/wiki/Potomac_River" title="Potomac River">Potomac River</a> into Maryland on September 5. Lincoln then restored Pope's troops to McClellan. McClellan and Lee fought at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Antietam" title="Battle of Antietam">Battle of Antietam</a> near <a href="/wiki/Sharpsburg,_Maryland" title="Sharpsburg, Maryland">Sharpsburg</a>, Maryland, on September 17, 1862, the bloodiest single day in United States military history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcPherson1988538.E2.80.9344_153-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcPherson1988538.E2.80.9344-153">[151]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcPherson1988543.E2.80.9345_155-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcPherson1988543.E2.80.9345-155">[153]</a></sup> Lee's army, checked at last, returned to Virginia before McClellan could destroy it. Antietam is considered a Union victory because it halted Lee's invasion of the North and provided an opportunity for Lincoln to announce his <a href="/wiki/Emancipation_Proclamation" title="Emancipation Proclamation">Emancipation Proclamation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcPherson1988557.E2.80.93558_156-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcPherson1988557.E2.80.93558-156">[154]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bayonet-charge-1250.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="879" data-file-width="1250" height="155" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Bayonet-charge-1250.jpg/220px-Bayonet-charge-1250.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Bayonet-charge-1250.jpg/330px-Bayonet-charge-1250.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Bayonet-charge-1250.jpg/440px-Bayonet-charge-1250.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bayonet-charge-1250.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Union forces performing a bayonet charge, 1862</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>When the cautious McClellan failed to follow up on Antietam, he was replaced by Maj. Gen. <a href="/wiki/Ambrose_Burnside" title="Ambrose Burnside">Ambrose Burnside</a>. Burnside was soon defeated at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Fredericksburg" title="Battle of Fredericksburg">Battle of Fredericksburg</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcPherson1988571.E2.80.9374_157-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcPherson1988571.E2.80.9374-157">[155]</a></sup> on December 13, 1862, when more than 12,000 Union soldiers were killed or wounded during repeated futile frontal assaults against Marye's Heights. After the battle, Burnside was replaced by Maj. Gen. <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Hooker" title="Joseph Hooker">Joseph Hooker</a>.</p>
<p>Hooker, too, proved unable to defeat Lee's army; despite outnumbering the Confederates by more than two to one, he was humiliated in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Chancellorsville" title="Battle of Chancellorsville">Battle of Chancellorsville</a> in May 1863.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcPherson1988639.E2.80.9345_158-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcPherson1988639.E2.80.9345-158">[156]</a></sup> Gen. Stonewall Jackson was shot in the arm by accidental friendly fire during the battle and subsequently died of complications.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[157]</a></sup> Gen. Hooker was replaced by Maj. Gen. <a href="/wiki/George_Meade" title="George Meade">George Meade</a> during Lee's second invasion of the North, in June. Meade defeated Lee at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Gettysburg" title="Battle of Gettysburg">Battle of Gettysburg</a> (July 1 to 3, 1863).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcPherson1988653.E2.80.93663_160-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcPherson1988653.E2.80.93663-160">[158]</a></sup> This was the bloodiest battle of the war, and has been called the war's <a href="/wiki/Turning_point_of_the_American_Civil_War" title="Turning point of the American Civil War">turning point</a>. <a href="/wiki/Pickett%27s_Charge" title="Pickett's Charge">Pickett's Charge</a> on July 3 is often considered the <a href="/wiki/High-water_mark_of_the_Confederacy" title="High-water mark of the Confederacy">high-water mark of the Confederacy</a> because it signaled the collapse of serious Confederate threats of victory. Lee's army suffered 28,000 casualties (versus Meade's 23,000).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcPherson1988664_161-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcPherson1988664-161">[159]</a></sup> However, Lincoln was angry that Meade failed to intercept Lee's retreat, and after Meade's inconclusive fall campaign, Lincoln turned to the Western Theater for new leadership. At the same time, the Confederate stronghold of Vicksburg surrendered, giving the Union control of the Mississippi River, permanently isolating the western Confederacy, and producing the new leader Lincoln needed, <a href="/wiki/Ulysses_S._Grant" title="Ulysses S. Grant">Ulysses S. Grant</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Western_theater">Western theater</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">For more details on this topic, see <a href="/wiki/Western_Theater_of_the_American_Civil_War" title="Western Theater of the American Civil War">Western Theater of the American Civil War</a>.</div>
<p>While the Confederate forces had numerous successes in the Eastern Theater, they were defeated many times in the West. They were driven from Missouri early in the war as a result of the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Pea_Ridge" title="Battle of Pea Ridge">Battle of Pea Ridge</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcPherson1988404.E2.80.9305_162-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcPherson1988404.E2.80.9305-162">[160]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Leonidas_Polk" title="Leonidas Polk">Leonidas Polk</a>'s invasion of <a href="/wiki/Columbus,_Kentucky" title="Columbus, Kentucky">Columbus</a>, Kentucky ended Kentucky's policy of neutrality and turned that state against the Confederacy. <a href="/wiki/Nashville,_Tennessee" title="Nashville, Tennessee">Nashville</a> and central <a href="/wiki/Tennessee" title="Tennessee">Tennessee</a> fell to the Union early in 1862, leading to attrition of local food supplies and livestock and a breakdown in social organization.</p>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:448px;max-width:448px">
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:222px;max-width:222px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Chickamauga.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1293" data-file-width="1781" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Chickamauga.jpg/220px-Chickamauga.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Chickamauga.jpg/330px-Chickamauga.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Chickamauga.jpg/440px-Chickamauga.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:222px;max-width:222px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:New_Orleans_h76369k.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="529" data-file-width="740" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/New_Orleans_h76369k.jpg/220px-New_Orleans_h76369k.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/New_Orleans_h76369k.jpg/330px-New_Orleans_h76369k.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/New_Orleans_h76369k.jpg/440px-New_Orleans_h76369k.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a></div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent">
<div class="center" style="width:auto; margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;">Left: The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Chickamauga" title="Battle of Chickamauga">Battle of Chickamauga</a>, the highest two-day losses. Confederate victory held off Union offensive for two months.</div>
<div class="center" style="width:auto; margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;">Right: <a href="/wiki/Capture_of_New_Orleans#New_Orleans_takes_a_stand" title="Capture of New Orleans">New Orleans captured</a>. Union ironclads forced passage, sank Confederate fleet, destroyed batteries, held docks for Army.</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_River" title="Mississippi River">Mississippi</a> was opened to Union traffic to the southern border of Tennessee with the taking of <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Island_Number_Ten" title="Battle of Island Number Ten">Island No. 10</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_Madrid,_Missouri" title="New Madrid, Missouri">New Madrid</a>, Missouri, and then <a href="/wiki/Memphis,_Tennessee" title="Memphis, Tennessee">Memphis, Tennessee</a>. In April 1862, the <a href="/wiki/Union_Navy" title="Union Navy">Union Navy</a> captured New Orleans,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcPherson1988418.E2.80.9320_163-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcPherson1988418.E2.80.9320-163">[161]</a></sup> which allowed Union forces to begin moving up the Mississippi. Only the fortress city of <a href="/wiki/Vicksburg,_Mississippi" title="Vicksburg, Mississippi">Vicksburg</a>, Mississippi, prevented Union control of the entire river.</p>
<p>General <a href="/wiki/Braxton_Bragg" title="Braxton Bragg">Braxton Bragg</a>'s second Confederate invasion of Kentucky ended with a meaningless victory over Maj. Gen. <a href="/wiki/Don_Carlos_Buell" title="Don Carlos Buell">Don Carlos Buell</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Perryville" title="Battle of Perryville">Battle of Perryville</a>, although Bragg was forced to end his attempt at invading Kentucky and retreat due to lack of support for the Confederacy in that state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcPherson1988419.E2.80.9320_164-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcPherson1988419.E2.80.9320-164">[162]</a></sup> Bragg was narrowly defeated by Maj. Gen. <a href="/wiki/William_Rosecrans" title="William Rosecrans">William Rosecrans</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Stones_River" title="Battle of Stones River">Battle of Stones River</a> in <a href="/wiki/Tennessee" title="Tennessee">Tennessee</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcPherson1988480.E2.80.9383_165-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcPherson1988480.E2.80.9383-165">[163]</a></sup></p>
<p>The one clear Confederate victory in the West was the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Chickamauga" title="Battle of Chickamauga">Battle of Chickamauga</a>. Bragg, reinforced by Lt. Gen. <a href="/wiki/James_Longstreet" title="James Longstreet">James Longstreet</a>'s corps (from Lee's army in the east), defeated Rosecrans, despite the heroic defensive stand of Maj. Gen. <a href="/wiki/George_Henry_Thomas" title="George Henry Thomas">George Henry Thomas</a>. Rosecrans retreated to <a href="/wiki/Chattanooga,_Tennessee" title="Chattanooga, Tennessee">Chattanooga</a>, which Bragg then besieged.</p>
<p>The Union's key strategist and tactician in the West was <a href="/wiki/Ulysses_S._Grant" title="Ulysses S. Grant">Ulysses S. Grant</a>, who won victories at Forts <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Fort_Henry" title="Battle of Fort Henry">Henry</a> and <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Fort_Donelson" title="Battle of Fort Donelson">Donelson</a> (by which the Union seized control of the <a href="/wiki/Tennessee_River" title="Tennessee River">Tennessee</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cumberland_River" title="Cumberland River">Cumberland</a> Rivers); the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Shiloh" title="Battle of Shiloh">Battle of Shiloh</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcPherson1988405.E2.80.9313_166-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcPherson1988405.E2.80.9313-166">[164]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Vicksburg" title="Siege of Vicksburg">Battle of Vicksburg</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcPherson1988637.E2.80.9338_167-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcPherson1988637.E2.80.9338-167">[165]</a></sup> which cemented Union control of the Mississippi River and is considered one of the <a href="/wiki/Turning_point_of_the_American_Civil_War" title="Turning point of the American Civil War">turning points</a> of the war. Grant marched to the relief of Rosecrans and defeated Bragg at the <a href="/wiki/Chattanooga_Campaign" title="Chattanooga Campaign">Third Battle of Chattanooga</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcPherson1988677.E2.80.9380_168-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcPherson1988677.E2.80.9380-168">[166]</a></sup> driving Confederate forces out of Tennessee and opening a route to Atlanta and the heart of the Confederacy.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Trans-Mississippi">Trans-Mississippi</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">For more details on Missouri in the Civil War, see <a href="/wiki/Trans-Mississippi_Theater_of_the_American_Civil_War" title="Trans-Mississippi Theater of the American Civil War">Trans-Mississippi Theater of the American Civil War</a>.</div>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:448px;max-width:448px">
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:222px;max-width:222px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Lawrence.png"><img alt="" data-file-height="586" data-file-width="900" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Battle_of_Lawrence.png/220px-Battle_of_Lawrence.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Battle_of_Lawrence.png/330px-Battle_of_Lawrence.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Battle_of_Lawrence.png/440px-Battle_of_Lawrence.png 2x" width="220"/></a></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:222px;max-width:222px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wilson%27s_Creek_charge_of_1st_Iowa.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="531" data-file-width="830" height="141" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Wilson%27s_Creek_charge_of_1st_Iowa.jpg/220px-Wilson%27s_Creek_charge_of_1st_Iowa.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Wilson%27s_Creek_charge_of_1st_Iowa.jpg/330px-Wilson%27s_Creek_charge_of_1st_Iowa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Wilson%27s_Creek_charge_of_1st_Iowa.jpg/440px-Wilson%27s_Creek_charge_of_1st_Iowa.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a></div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent">
<div class="center" style="width:auto; margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;">Left: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lawrence_Massacre" title="Lawrence Massacre">Quantrill's Raid</a> captured a hotel in free-state Kansas for a day in a town of 2,000, burned 185 buildings, killed 182 men and boys.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKeegan2009270_169-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKeegan2009270-169">[167]</a></sup></div>
<div class="center" style="width:auto; margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;">Right: <a href="/wiki/Nathaniel_Lyon" title="Nathaniel Lyon">Nathaniel Lyon</a> secured St. Louis docks and arsenal, led Union forces to expel Missouri Confederate forces and government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKeegan2009100_170-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKeegan2009100-170">[168]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Extensive <a href="/wiki/Guerrilla_warfare" title="Guerrilla warfare">guerrilla warfare</a> characterized the trans-Mississippi region, as the Confederacy lacked the troops and the logistics to support regular armies that could challenge Union control.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[169]</a></sup> Roving Confederate bands such as <a href="/wiki/Quantrill%27s_Raiders" title="Quantrill's Raiders">Quantrill's Raiders</a> terrorized the countryside, striking both military installations and civilian settlements.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[170]</a></sup> The "Sons of Liberty" and "Order of the American Knights" attacked pro-Union people, elected officeholders, and unarmed uniformed soldiers. These partisans could not be entirely driven out of the state of Missouri until an entire regular Union infantry division was engaged.</p>
<p>By 1864, these violent activities harmed the nationwide anti-war movement organizing against the re-election of Lincoln. Missouri not only stayed in the Union, Lincoln took 70 percent of the vote for re-election.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKeegan2009270_169-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKeegan2009270-169">[167]</a></sup></p>
<p>Numerous small-scale military actions south and west of Missouri sought to control <a href="/wiki/Indian_Territory_in_the_American_Civil_War" title="Indian Territory in the American Civil War">Indian Territory</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_Mexico_Territory_in_the_American_Civil_War" title="New Mexico Territory in the American Civil War">New Mexico Territory</a> for the Union. The Union repulsed Confederate incursions into New Mexico in 1862, and the exiled Arizona government withdrew into Texas. In the Indian Territory, civil war broke out within tribes. About 12,000 Indian warriors fought for the Confederacy, and smaller numbers for the Union.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[171]</a></sup> The most prominent Cherokee was Brigadier General <a href="/wiki/Stand_Watie" title="Stand Watie">Stand Watie</a>, the last Confederate general to surrender.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[172]</a></sup></p>
<p>After the fall of <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Vicksburg" title="Siege of Vicksburg">Vicksburg</a> in July 1863, General <a href="/wiki/Edmund_Kirby_Smith" title="Edmund Kirby Smith">Kirby Smith</a> in Texas was informed by Jefferson Davis that he could expect no further help from east of the Mississippi River. Although he lacked resources to beat Union armies, he built up a formidable arsenal at Tyler, along with his own Kirby Smithdom economy, a virtual "independent fiefdom" in Texas, including railroad construction and international smuggling. The Union in turn did not directly engage him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKeegan2009220.E2.80.9321_175-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKeegan2009220.E2.80.9321-175">[173]</a></sup> Its 1864 <a href="/wiki/Red_River_Campaign" title="Red River Campaign">Red River Campaign</a> to take Shreveport, Louisiana was a failure and Texas remained in Confederate hands throughout the war.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="End_of_the_war">End of the war</span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Conquest_of_Virginia">Conquest of Virginia</span></h4>
<p>At the beginning of 1864, Lincoln made Grant commander of all Union armies. Grant made his headquarters with the Army of the Potomac, and put Maj. Gen. <a href="/wiki/William_Tecumseh_Sherman" title="William Tecumseh Sherman">William Tecumseh Sherman</a> in command of most of the western armies. Grant understood the concept of <a href="/wiki/Total_war" title="Total war">total war</a> and believed, along with Lincoln and Sherman, that only the utter defeat of Confederate forces and their economic base would end the war.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-history_176-0"><a href="#cite_note-history-176">[174]</a></sup> This was total war not in killing civilians but rather in taking provisions and forage and destroying homes, farms, and railroads, that Grant said "would otherwise have gone to the support of secession and rebellion. This policy I believe exercised a material influence in hastening the end."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[175]</a></sup> Grant devised a coordinated strategy that would strike at the entire Confederacy from multiple directions. Generals <a href="/wiki/George_Meade" title="George Meade">George Meade</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Benjamin_Butler_(politician)" title="Benjamin Butler (politician)">Benjamin Butler</a> were ordered to move against Lee near Richmond, General <a href="/wiki/Franz_Sigel" title="Franz Sigel">Franz Sigel</a> (and later <a href="/wiki/Philip_Sheridan" title="Philip Sheridan">Philip Sheridan</a>) were to <a href="/wiki/Valley_Campaigns_of_1864" title="Valley Campaigns of 1864">attack the Shenandoah Valley</a>, General Sherman was to capture Atlanta and march to the sea (the Atlantic Ocean), Generals <a href="/wiki/George_Crook" title="George Crook">George Crook</a> and <a href="/wiki/William_W._Averell" title="William W. Averell">William W. Averell</a> were to operate against railroad supply lines in <a href="/wiki/West_Virginia" title="West Virginia">West Virginia</a>, and Maj. Gen. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nathaniel_Prentice_Banks" title="Nathaniel Prentice Banks">Nathaniel P. Banks</a> was to capture <a href="/wiki/Mobile,_Alabama" title="Mobile, Alabama">Mobile</a>, Alabama.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[176]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:EwellsDeadSpotsylvania1864crop01.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1105" data-file-width="1250" height="194" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/EwellsDeadSpotsylvania1864crop01.jpg/220px-EwellsDeadSpotsylvania1864crop01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/EwellsDeadSpotsylvania1864crop01.jpg/330px-EwellsDeadSpotsylvania1864crop01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/EwellsDeadSpotsylvania1864crop01.jpg/440px-EwellsDeadSpotsylvania1864crop01.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:EwellsDeadSpotsylvania1864crop01.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
These dead soldiersâfrom <a href="/wiki/Richard_S._Ewell" title="Richard S. Ewell">Ewell</a>'s May 1864 attack at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battle_of_Spotsylvania" title="Battle of Spotsylvania">Spotsylvania</a>âdelayed Grant's advance on Richmond in the <a href="/wiki/Overland_Campaign" title="Overland Campaign">Overland Campaign</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Peacemakers_1868.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2254" data-file-width="3000" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/The_Peacemakers_1868.jpg/220px-The_Peacemakers_1868.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/The_Peacemakers_1868.jpg/330px-The_Peacemakers_1868.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/The_Peacemakers_1868.jpg/440px-The_Peacemakers_1868.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Peacemakers_1868.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i><a href="/wiki/The_Peacemakers" title="The Peacemakers">The Peacemakers</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/George_Peter_Alexander_Healy" title="George Peter Alexander Healy">George Peter Alexander Healy</a> portrays <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/William_T._Sherman" title="William T. Sherman">Sherman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ulysses_S._Grant" title="Ulysses S. Grant">Grant</a>, <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Lincoln" title="Abraham Lincoln">Lincoln</a>, and <a href="/wiki/David_Dixon_Porter" title="David Dixon Porter">Porter</a> discussing plans for the last weeks of the Civil War aboard the steamer <i><a href="/wiki/River_Queen_(steamboat)" title="River Queen (steamboat)">River Queen</a></i> in March 1865.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Grant's army set out on the <a href="/wiki/Overland_Campaign" title="Overland Campaign">Overland Campaign</a> with the goal of drawing Lee into a defense of Richmond, where they would attempt to pin down and destroy the Confederate army. The Union army first attempted to maneuver past Lee and fought several battles, notably at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Wilderness" title="Battle of the Wilderness">Wilderness</a>, <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Spotsylvania_Court_House" title="Battle of Spotsylvania Court House">Spotsylvania</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Cold_Harbor" title="Battle of Cold Harbor">Cold Harbor</a>. These battles resulted in heavy losses on both sides, and forced Lee's Confederates to fall back repeatedly. An attempt to outflank Lee from the south failed under Butler, who was trapped inside the <a href="/wiki/Bermuda_Hundred_Campaign" title="Bermuda Hundred Campaign">Bermuda Hundred</a> river bend. Each battle resulted in setbacks for the Union that mirrored what they had suffered under prior generals, though unlike those prior generals, Grant fought on rather than retreat. Grant was tenacious and kept pressing Lee's Army of Northern Virginia back to Richmond. While Lee was preparing for an attack on Richmond, Grant unexpectedly turned south to cross the <a href="/wiki/James_River" title="James River">James River</a> and began the protracted <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Petersburg" title="Siege of Petersburg">Siege of Petersburg</a>, where the two armies engaged in <a href="/wiki/Trench_warfare" title="Trench warfare">trench warfare</a> for over nine months.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcPherson1988724.E2.80.9342_179-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcPherson1988724.E2.80.9342-179">[177]</a></sup></p>
<p>Grant finally found a commander, General <a href="/wiki/Philip_Sheridan" title="Philip Sheridan">Philip Sheridan</a>, aggressive enough to prevail in the <a href="/wiki/Valley_Campaigns_of_1864" title="Valley Campaigns of 1864">Valley Campaigns of 1864</a>. Sheridan was initially repelled at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_New_Market" title="Battle of New Market">Battle of New Market</a> by former U.S. Vice President and Confederate Gen. <a href="/wiki/John_C._Breckinridge" title="John C. Breckinridge">John C. Breckinridge</a>. The Battle of New Market was the Confederacy's last major victory of the war. After redoubling his efforts, Sheridan defeated Maj. Gen. <a href="/wiki/Jubal_Early" title="Jubal Early">Jubal A. Early</a> in a series of battles, including a final decisive defeat at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Cedar_Creek" title="Battle of Cedar Creek">Battle of Cedar Creek</a>. Sheridan then proceeded to destroy the agricultural base of the <a href="/wiki/Shenandoah_Valley" title="Shenandoah Valley">Shenandoah Valley</a>, a strategy similar to the tactics Sherman later employed in Georgia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcPherson1988778.E2.80.9379_180-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcPherson1988778.E2.80.9379-180">[178]</a></sup></p>
<p>Meanwhile, Sherman maneuvered from Chattanooga to Atlanta, defeating Confederate Generals <a href="/wiki/Joseph_E._Johnston" title="Joseph E. Johnston">Joseph E. Johnston</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Bell_Hood" title="John Bell Hood">John Bell Hood</a> along the way. The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Atlanta" title="Battle of Atlanta">fall of Atlanta</a> on September 2, 1864, guaranteed the reelection of Lincoln as president.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcPherson1988773.E2.80.9376_181-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcPherson1988773.E2.80.9376-181">[179]</a></sup> Hood left the Atlanta area to swing around and menace Sherman's supply lines and invade Tennessee in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Franklin-Nashville_Campaign" title="Franklin-Nashville Campaign">Franklin-Nashville Campaign</a>. Union Maj. Gen. <a href="/wiki/John_Schofield" title="John Schofield">John Schofield</a> defeated Hood at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Franklin_(1864)" title="Battle of Franklin (1864)">Battle of Franklin</a>, and <a href="/wiki/George_Henry_Thomas" title="George Henry Thomas">George H. Thomas</a> dealt Hood a massive defeat at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Nashville" title="Battle of Nashville">Battle of Nashville</a>, effectively destroying Hood's army.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcPherson1988812.E2.80.9315_182-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcPherson1988812.E2.80.9315-182">[180]</a></sup></p>
<p>Leaving Atlanta, and his base of supplies, Sherman's army marched with an unknown destination, laying waste to about 20 percent of the farms in Georgia in his "<a href="/wiki/Sherman%27s_March_to_the_Sea" title="Sherman's March to the Sea">March to the Sea</a>". He reached the Atlantic Ocean at <a href="/wiki/Savannah,_Georgia" title="Savannah, Georgia">Savannah</a>, Georgia in December 1864. Sherman's army was followed by thousands of freed slaves; there were no major battles along the March. Sherman turned north through South Carolina and North Carolina to approach the Confederate Virginia lines from the south, increasing the pressure on Lee's army.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcPherson1988825.E2.80.9330_183-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcPherson1988825.E2.80.9330-183">[181]</a></sup></p>
<p>Lee's army, thinned by desertion and casualties, was now much smaller than Grant's. One last Confederate attempt to break the Union hold on Petersburg failed at the decisive <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Five_Forks" title="Battle of Five Forks">Battle of Five Forks</a> (sometimes called "the <a href="/wiki/Waterloo_in_popular_culture#Other" title="Waterloo in popular culture">Waterloo</a> of the Confederacy") on April 1. This meant that the Union now controlled the entire perimeter surrounding Richmond-Petersburg, completely cutting it off from the Confederacy. Realizing that the capital was now lost, Lee decided to evacuate his army. The Confederate capital fell to the <a href="/wiki/XXV_Corps_(Union_Army)" title="XXV Corps (Union Army)">Union XXV Corps</a>, composed of black troops. The remaining Confederate units fled west after a defeat at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battle_of_Sayler%27s_Creek" title="Battle of Sayler's Creek">Sayler's Creek</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcPherson1988846.E2.80.9347_184-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcPherson1988846.E2.80.9347-184">[182]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Confederacy_surrenders">Confederacy surrenders</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Civil_war_1861-1865.jpg"><img alt="A map of the U.S. South showing shrinking territory under rebel control" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="898" data-file-width="1357" height="199" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Civil_war_1861-1865.jpg/300px-Civil_war_1861-1865.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Civil_war_1861-1865.jpg/450px-Civil_war_1861-1865.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Civil_war_1861-1865.jpg/600px-Civil_war_1861-1865.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Civil_war_1861-1865.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Map of Confederate territory losses year by year</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Conclusion_of_the_American_Civil_War" title="Conclusion of the American Civil War">Conclusion of the American Civil War</a></div>
<p>Initially, Lee did not intend to surrender, but planned to regroup at the <a href="/wiki/Appomattox_Court_House_National_Historical_Park" title="Appomattox Court House National Historical Park">village of Appomattox Court House</a>, where supplies were to be waiting, and then continue the war. Grant chased Lee and got in front of him, so that when Lee's army reached Appomattox Court House, they were surrounded. After an initial battle, Lee decided that the fight was now hopeless, and surrendered his Army of Northern Virginia on April 9, 1865, at the <a href="/wiki/McLean_House_(Appomattox,_Virginia)" title="McLean House (Appomattox, Virginia)">McLean House</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-appomattox_185-0"><a href="#cite_note-appomattox-185">[183]</a></sup> In an untraditional gesture and as a sign of Grant's respect and anticipation of peacefully restoring Confederate states to the Union, Lee was permitted to keep his sword and his horse, <a href="/wiki/Traveller_(horse)" title="Traveller (horse)">Traveller</a>.</p>
<p>On April 14, 1865, President Lincoln was <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abraham_Lincoln_assassination" title="Abraham Lincoln assassination">shot</a> by <a href="/wiki/John_Wilkes_Booth" title="John Wilkes Booth">John Wilkes Booth</a>, a Southern sympathizer. Lincoln died early the next morning, and <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Johnson" title="Andrew Johnson">Andrew Johnson</a> became the president. Meanwhile, Confederate forces across the South surrendered as news of Lee's surrender reached them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-surrender_186-0"><a href="#cite_note-surrender-186">[184]</a></sup> On April 26, 1865, General <a href="/wiki/Joseph_E._Johnston" title="Joseph E. Johnston">Joseph E. Johnston</a> surrendered nearly 90,000 men of the <a href="/wiki/Army_of_Tennessee" title="Army of Tennessee">Army of Tennessee</a> to Major General <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/William_T._Sherman" title="William T. Sherman">William T. Sherman</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Bennett_Place" title="Bennett Place">Bennett Place</a> near present-day Durham, North Carolina. It proved to be the largest surrender of Confederate forces, effectively bringing the war to an end. President Johnson officially declared a virtual end to the insurrection on May 9, 1865; President <a href="/wiki/Jefferson_Davis" title="Jefferson Davis">Jefferson Davis</a> was captured the following day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT_JD_Cap_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-NYT_JD_Cap-1">[1]</a></sup> On June 2, Kirby Smith officially surrendered his troops in the Trans-Mississippi Department.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[185]</a></sup> On June 23, Cherokee leader <a href="/wiki/Stand_Watie" title="Stand Watie">Stand Watie</a> became the last Confederate General to surrender his forces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[186]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Diplomacy">Diplomacy</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Diplomacy_of_the_American_Civil_War" title="Diplomacy of the American Civil War">Diplomacy of the American Civil War</a></div>
<p>Though the Confederacy hoped that Britain and France would join them against the Union, this was never likely, and so they instead tried to bring Britain and France in as mediators.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcPherson1988546.E2.80.9357_189-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcPherson1988546.E2.80.9357-189">[187]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHerring2011237_190-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerring2011237-190">[188]</a></sup> The Union, under Lincoln and Secretary of State <a href="/wiki/William_H._Seward" title="William H. Seward">William H. Seward</a> worked to block this, and threatened war if any country officially recognized the existence of the Confederate States of America. In 1861, Southerners voluntarily embargoed cotton shipments, hoping to start an economic depression in Europe that would force Britain to enter the war to get cotton, but this did not work. Worse, Europe developed other cotton suppliers, which they found superior, hindering the South's recovery after the war.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcPherson1988386_191-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcPherson1988386-191">[189]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:284px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:USS_Wissahickon_Crewmembers.jpg"><img alt="A group of twenty-six sailors posing around a rifled naval cannon" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="652" data-file-width="1200" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/USS_Wissahickon_Crewmembers.jpg/282px-USS_Wissahickon_Crewmembers.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/USS_Wissahickon_Crewmembers.jpg/423px-USS_Wissahickon_Crewmembers.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/USS_Wissahickon_Crewmembers.jpg/564px-USS_Wissahickon_Crewmembers.jpg 2x" width="282"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:USS_Wissahickon_Crewmembers.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Crewmembers of <a href="/wiki/USS_Wissahickon_(1861)" title="USS Wissahickon (1861)">USS <i>Wissahickon</i></a> by the ship's 11-inch (280Â mm) <a href="/wiki/Dahlgren_gun" title="Dahlgren gun">Dahlgren gun</a>, circa 1863</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Cotton_diplomacy" title="Cotton diplomacy">Cotton diplomacy</a> proved a failure as Europe had a surplus of cotton, while the 1860â62 crop failures in Europe made the North's grain exports of critical importance. It also helped to turn European opinion further away from the Confederacy. It was said that "King Corn was more powerful than King Cotton", as U.S. grain went from a quarter of the British import trade to almost half.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcPherson1988386_191-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcPherson1988386-191">[189]</a></sup> When Britain did face a cotton shortage, it was temporary, being replaced by increased cultivation in Egypt and India. Meanwhile, the war created employment for arms makers, ironworkers, and British ships to transport weapons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nevins73_192-0"><a href="#cite_note-nevins73-192">[190]</a></sup></p>
<p>Lincoln's foreign policy was deficient in 1861 in terms of appealing to European public opinion. Diplomats had to explain that United States was not committed to the ending of slavery, but instead they repeated legalistic arguments about the unconstitutionality of secession. Confederate spokesmen, on the other hand, were much more successful by ignoring slavery and instead focusing on their struggle for liberty, their commitment to free trade, and the essential role of cotton in the European economy. In addition, the European aristocracy (the dominant factor in every major country) was "absolutely gleeful in pronouncing the American debacle as proof that the entire experiment in popular government had failed. European government leaders welcomed the fragmentation of the ascendant American Republic."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193">[191]</a></sup></p>
<p>U.S. <a href="/wiki/Ambassador" title="Ambassador">minister</a> to Britain <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Charles_Francis_Adams,_Sr." title="Charles Francis Adams, Sr.">Charles Francis Adams</a> proved particularly adept and convinced Britain not to boldly challenge the blockade. The Confederacy purchased several warships from commercial shipbuilders in Britain (<a href="/wiki/CSS_Alabama" title="CSS Alabama">CSS <i>Alabama</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/CSS_Shenandoah" title="CSS Shenandoah">CSS <i>Shenandoah</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/CSS_Tennessee_(1863)" title="CSS Tennessee (1863)">CSS <i>Tennessee</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/CSS_Tallahassee" title="CSS Tallahassee">CSS <i>Tallahassee</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/CSS_Florida" title="CSS Florida">CSS <i>Florida</i></a>, and some others). The most famous, the <a href="/wiki/CSS_Alabama" title="CSS Alabama">CSS <i>Alabama</i></a>, did considerable damage and led to serious <a href="/wiki/Alabama_Claims" title="Alabama Claims">postwar disputes</a>. However, public opinion against slavery created a political liability for politicians in Britain, where the antislavery movement was powerful.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194">[192]</a></sup></p>
<p>War loomed in late 1861 between the U.S. and Britain over the <a href="/wiki/Trent_Affair" title="Trent Affair"><i>Trent</i> affair</a>, involving the U.S. Navy's boarding of the British ship <a href="/wiki/RMS_Trent" title="RMS Trent"><i>Trent</i></a> and seizure of two Confederate diplomats. However, London and Washington were able to smooth over the problem after Lincoln released the two. In 1862, the British considered mediation between North and Southâ though even such an offer would have risked war with the U.S. British Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Henry_John_Temple,_3rd_Viscount_Palmerston" title="Henry John Temple, 3rd Viscount Palmerston">Lord Palmerston</a> reportedly read <i><a href="/wiki/Uncle_Tom%27s_Cabin" title="Uncle Tom's Cabin">Uncle Tom's Cabin</a></i> three times when deciding on this.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-approaching_195-0"><a href="#cite_note-approaching-195">[193]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Union victory in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Antietam" title="Battle of Antietam">Battle of Antietam</a> caused them to delay this decision. The <a href="/wiki/Emancipation_Proclamation" title="Emancipation Proclamation">Emancipation Proclamation</a> over time would reinforce the political liability of supporting the Confederacy. Despite sympathy for the Confederacy, France's own <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_intervention_in_Mexico" title="French intervention in Mexico">seizure of Mexico</a> ultimately deterred them from war with the Union. Confederate offers late in the war to end slavery in return for diplomatic recognition were not seriously considered by London or Paris. After 1863, the <a href="/wiki/January_Uprising" title="January Uprising">Polish revolt against Russia</a> further distracted the European powers, and ensured that they would remain neutral.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHerring2011261_196-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerring2011261-196">[194]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Union_victory_and_aftermath">Union victory and aftermath</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Results">Results</span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Origins_of_the_American_Civil_War" title="Origins of the American Civil War">causes of the war</a>, the reasons for its outcome, and even <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Naming_the_American_Civil_War" title="Naming the American Civil War">the name of the war itself</a> are subjects of lingering contention today. The North and West grew rich while the once-rich South became poor for a century. The national political power of the slaveowners and rich southerners ended. Historians are less sure about the results of the postwar Reconstruction, especially regarding the second class citizenship of the Freedmen and their poverty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcPherson1988851_197-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcPherson1988851-197">[195]</a></sup></p>
<p>Historians have debated whether the Confederacy could have won the war. Most scholars, including <a href="/wiki/James_M._McPherson" title="James M. McPherson">James McPherson</a>, argue that Confederate victory was at least possible.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcPherson1988855_198-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcPherson1988855-198">[196]</a></sup> McPherson argues that the North's advantage in population and resources made Northern victory likely but not guaranteed. He also argues that if the Confederacy had fought using unconventional tactics, they would have more easily been able to hold out long enough to exhaust the Union.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-confederacy_199-0"><a href="#cite_note-confederacy-199">[197]</a></sup></p>
<table class="wikitable" style="float:right; text-align:center; margin:2em;">
